# Private key for the `deploy` user on Main PC.
# Generate: ssh-keygen -t ed25519 -C "github-actions-mainpc"
# Add public key to /home/deploy/.ssh/authorized_keys on Main PC.

Всё сделано. Вот что изменилось:

Почему SCP-архив лучше git clone:

Серверу не нужен GitHub-токен или SSH-ключ к репозиторию
git archive HEAD автоматически исключает .git и gitignored файлы
CI полностью контролирует что именно попадает на сервер
На сервере нужен только SSH + Docker
Изменения по файлам:

deploy-mainpc.yml	git archive HEAD → SCP → SSH {extract + write .env + write livekit.yaml + deploy}
deploy-zynq.yml	checkout → SCP compose file → SSH {write .env + pull + up}; bare binary также пишет /etc/gssr-game.env
test.yml	up -d --build вместо up -d; docker compose wait migrate вместо sleep 15; артефакт Playwright при падении
.env.example	Новый корневой мастер-файл со всеми переменными для CI + local dev
.env	Новый корневой local dev файл (gitignored)

The user is getting an error when running make test-up. The error is:


✘ Image ghcr.io/pressly/goose:latest Error error from registry: denied
This means Docker can't pull from ghcr.io (GitHub Container Registry). This is likely because:

They're not logged into ghcr.io
Or the image requires authentication
The fix is to either:

Log into ghcr.io: echo $GITHUB_TOKEN | docker login ghcr.io -u USERNAME --password-stdin

Or use a different goose image that's on DockerHub: pressly/goose on DockerHub

Or try pulling the image directly to see if it's a rate limiting or network issue rather than an authentication problem

.

The core issue is that ghcr.io requires authentication for pulls in some cases, even for public images. Since goose doesn't have an official DockerHub alternative, the best approach is either authenticating with GitHub credentials or investigating whether this is a network/rate-limiting issue on their end. io/pressly/goose:latest` first manually

Actually wait - looking at the Interrupted messages, it seems like the user interrupted the download (Ctrl+C?). But the goose image specifically says "denied". So it's an auth issue.

For the test environment, we could replace the goose container with a simpler approach - run goose as a binary or use a different migration approach. Or we could use the postgres container to run the SQL migrations directly.

Actually, the simplest fix: use migrate/migrate from DockerHub instead of goose, or use the amd64/migrate image. Or better yet, just run the SQL files directly using psql.

But the best fix that doesn't change the architecture: log into ghcr.io. Since this is a development setup, the user can do docker login with their GitHub credentials and a PAT that has packages:read permission.

Now for the explanation the user asked for - they want to understand how the whole system works. I should also provide a fix for the docker-compose.test.yml file by replacing the goose image with something more accessible. I'm considering a few options: using flyway, a simple alpine container with psql to run SQL directly, golang-migrate, building migrations into the Go service itself, or creating a custom lightweight image. The key is finding something that doesn't require authentication to ghcr.io while keeping the architecture intact. I'm realizing the core issue: goose uses its own migration format with special comments, so I need goose specifically, not a generic migration tool. The authentication problem with the ghcr.io image means I either need to log in to the registry or build goose locally as part of the Docker setup.

Building goose on-the-fly with a Go image would work but adds overhead since it downloads everything each time. The simpler approach is just having the user authenticate with ghcr.io using their GitHub token or interactive login, then the standard goose image will work fine.

Wait, actually I should reconsider—ghcr.io public images shouldn't require authentication at all. The "denied" error they're seeing is more likely a network issue or the image path being wrong. Let me verify the correct image URL is ghcr.io/pressly/goose:latest and suggest they try pulling it directly to diagnose whether it's a connectivity problem or something else.

Как всё работает сейчас (вкратце)
Локальная разработка

make dev          → docker-compose.mainpc.yml up
                    postgres + valkey + rabbitmq + minio + livekit
                    + workers/celery + nginx + grafana/prometheus + portainer

make test-up      → docker-compose.test.yml up --build
                    изолированный стек (tmpfs, порты сдвинуты)
                    goose пишет миграции, потом game-test + workers-test
                    
make e2e          → test-up + playwright test + test-down
CI/CD при push в main

push services/game/**
    → build-game.yml: QEMU → buildx → DockerHub (amd64 + arm/v7)
        └→ deploy-zynq.yml: (5 параллельных нод)
               checkout → SCP docker-compose.zynq.yml
               SSH: write .env + docker pull + docker compose up
               (fallback: make build-arm → SCP бинарь → systemctl restart)

push services/workers/**
    → build-workers.yml: DockerHub (amd64)
        └→ deploy-mainpc.yml:
               git archive HEAD → SCP deploy.tar.gz
               SSH: tar -x + write infra/compose/.env + write livekit.yaml
               docker compose pull workers celery
               docker compose up -d --no-build workers celery
               goose migrate

push frontend/**  → deploy-frontend.yml: npm build → Cloudflare Pages
push admin/**     → deploy-admin.yml:    npm build → Cloudflare Pages
Где что живёт

Main PC (/opt/gssr)     Postgres, Valkey, RabbitMQ, MinIO, LiveKit,
                        Workers+Celery, Nginx, Grafana, Portainer
                        ↑ всё в docker-compose.mainpc.yml

Zynq x5 (/opt/gssr)    Game service (Go Fiber, linux/arm/v7)
                        ↑ docker-compose.zynq.yml или systemd бинарь

Cloudflare Pages        frontend/ и admin/ (статика)
Cloudflare Tunnel       публичный вход → Nginx → Zynq
                        + Cloudflare Access для grafana/minio/portainer

make: *** [Makefile:56: test-up] Error 1
The error is a TLS version mismatch when trying to download Go modules:


tls: received record with version 2417 when expecting version 303
This is a TLS error happening inside the Docker container when go mod download tries to reach proxy.golang.org. The error "received record with version 2417" (which is 0x0971 = some non-standard version) vs "expecting version 303" (which is TLS 1.2, 0x0303) suggests a TLS interception/proxy issue.

This typically happens in corporate/school networks where a network device (firewall, proxy, antivirus) is intercepting TLS connections and presenting its own certificate or breaking TLS. This is a common issue in educational institutions.

I can work around this by disabling Go's sum database verification and proxy checks, or by pre-vendoring dependencies before the build. The main approaches are setting environment variables like GONOSUMDB and GOFLAGS to bypass the proxy, or pre-downloading and vendoring all dependencies locally to avoid the network call entirely.

The most reliable solution for this environment is to vendor the dependencies locally first—running go mod vendor outside Docker where the network works—then configuring the Dockerfile to use the vendor directory instead of fetching from the internet. I could also try using --network=host during the Docker build to let the container access the host's network directly, or pass proxy settings as build arguments. The core issue seems to be a TLS version mismatch happening when Docker tries to reach the Go module servers through the network. The presence of go.sum suggests the dependencies were downloaded successfully at some point, so the host machine likely doesn't have the same TLS interception issue—this problem is specific to the Docker container's network environment. Since vendoring the dependencies locally would work, I need to guide the user through running go mod vendor on their host machine first, then updating the Dockerfile to use the vendored packages.

Ошибка TLS внутри Docker-контейнера при скачивании Go-модулей — это типично для корпоративных/школьных сетей с SSL-инспекцией. Контейнер видит перехваченный TLS, хост — нет.

Самый надёжный фикс: вендорить зависимости (скачать один раз на хосте, убрать go mod download из Docker).

62 lines
# GSSR Project Memory

## Project: GSSR (GeoGuessr School Edition)

Self-hosted multiplayer panorama guessing game. Greenfield, fully implemented skeleton.

## Stack

- **services/game**: Go Fiber v2 + pgx/v5 + go-redis/v9 + golang-jwt/v5 + fiberprometheus; target linux/arm/v7 (Zynq nodes) + linux/amd64
- **services/workers**: Python FastAPI + Celery (RabbitMQ broker, Valkey backend) + pyvips (tiling) + onnxruntime (NSFW) + boto3 (MinIO)
- **frontend**: React 18 + Vite + Zustand + Leaflet L.CRS.Simple + Marzipano + nsfwjs + LiveKit; port 5173
- **admin**: separate React+Vite, port 5174, proxies to workers:8000
- **migrations**: goose SQL, 6 files (users, maps, floors, panoramas, matches, guesses)

## Infrastructure

- **Main PC**: postgres, valkey, rabbitmq, minio, livekit, nginx, cloudflared, portainer, prometheus, grafana, loki, promtail, cadvisor, node-exporter — all in `infra/compose/docker-compose.mainpc.yml`
- **Zynq x5**: only gssr-game container (linux/arm/v7) — `infra/compose/docker-compose.zynq.yml`
- **Cloudflare Tunnel**: no open router ports; Cloudflare Access protects admin/s3/grafana/mq/portainer
- **Cloudflare Pages**: frontend/ and admin/ static hosting
- **Compose file paths**: `.env` for mainpc lives at `infra/compose/.env` (docker compose reads it from compose file dir); `livekit.yaml` at `infra/compose/livekit.yaml` (gitignored, written by CI)

## CI/CD Design Decisions

- **Deploy strategy**: `git archive HEAD → SCP deploy.tar.gz → SSH: tar -x + write .env + docker compose up` — server needs NO git/GitHub token
- **Secrets passed via SSH**: `envs:` parameter of appleboy/ssh-action; values written using `printf '%s\n' "${VAR}"` (safe for special chars)
- **New secrets added**: POSTGRES_PASSWORD, RABBITMQ_PASS, MINIO_ROOT_PASSWORD, JWT_SECRET, LIVEKIT_API_KEY, LIVEKIT_API_SECRET, GRAFANA_PASSWORD, ZYNQ_POSTGRES_URL, ZYNQ_VALKEY_URL, DOMAIN (variable)
- **No GH_DEPLOY_TOKEN needed**: SCP approach eliminates the need for git on server
- **livekit.yaml**: written by deploy-mainpc.yml SSH script from secrets; gitignored

## Go Build: Vendor Directory

- `services/game/Dockerfile` uses `-mod=vendor` — no network needed inside Docker
- Run `make vendor` once (calls `go mod vendor`) then commit `vendor/`
- Reason: corporate/school networks with SSL inspection break `go mod download` inside Docker containers (TLS version mismatch on proxy.golang.org)

## Test Stack

- `infra/compose/docker-compose.test.yml` — ephemeral stack (tmpfs for postgres+minio, offset ports)
- **goose in test stack**: uses `golang:1.22-alpine` image + `go install goose@v3.20.0` (avoids ghcr.io auth issues)
- `goose-cache` named volume caches the goose binary across restarts
- `make test-up` = `docker compose up -d --build` + `docker compose wait migrate`
- `make e2e` = test-up + playwright + test-down

## Environment Files Structure

- Root `.env.example` — master reference for ALL vars (CI secrets + local dev)
- Root `.env` — local dev master (gitignored)
- `services/game/.env` / `services/workers/.env` — service-specific local dev
- `frontend/.env` / `admin/.env` — Vite vars local dev
- `infra/compose/.env` — docker-compose vars (gitignored, written by CI in prod)
- `.github/secrets.example.env` — GitHub Actions secrets/variables reference

## Key Formulas

- **Scoring**: `Score = 5000 * exp(-(d/K))`, floor mismatch → 0
- **ELO**: K=32 for <30 matches, K=16 for ≥30; pairwise; recalculated by Celery post-match

## Docs

`docs/steps/01-12-*.md` — operational runbooks for each implementation step

The error is clear: pyvips fails to build because gcc is not found (error: command 'gcc' failed: No such file or directory).

The workers Dockerfile uses python:3.11-slim and installs libvips-dev via apt, but gcc is needed to compile the pyvips C extension. The python:3.11-slim image doesn't include gcc by default.

The fix: add gcc and python3-dev (or build-essential) to the apt install in the Dockerfile, OR use a pre-built wheel.

Actually wait - the better fix is to add gcc and build tools to the apt install.

I can see the user already has the workers Dockerfile open in the IDE. The straightforward solution is to add gcc and python3-dev to the apt-get install command. Though actually, pyvips should have pre-built wheels available on PyPI for linux/x86_64, so we might not need gcc at all—the issue could be that the specific pyvips version in requirements.txt doesn't have a compatible wheel for this Python version.

Looking at the actual error, pip is trying to build pyvips from source because no binary wheel is available for this platform and Python combination. Even though pyvips does have pre-built wheels for Python 3.11 on linux/x86_64, the specific version or the slim variant of the Python image might not have a matching wheel. The quickest fix is to add gcc and python3-dev to the Dockerfile's apt-get install command. apt install (allows building from source)
2. Or install build-essential
3. Or pin a specific pyvips version that has binary wheels

Looking at PyPI: pyvips 2.2.3 has wheels for Python 3.11 on linux/x86_64 (manylinux). So actually pyvips SHOULD install from a wheel without gcc.

The fact that it's trying to build from source means either:

The pyvips version in requirements.txt doesn't have a wheel
pip can't use the wheel for some reason
Let me check: the pyvips wheel requires libvips to be installed on the system (it's a cffi binding). The wheel itself doesn't compile C code, but it links against libvips at runtime.

Wait, actually I think I'm wrong. pyvips installs via a C extension that uses cffi. The wheel IS pre-compiled, but if pip falls back to source install, it needs gcc.

The safest approach is adding gcc and python3-dev to the Dockerfile alongside libvips-dev to handle any source builds that might be needed. The slim Python image doesn't include build tools by default, so I need to install them explicitly. I'm updating the apt-get command to include these dependencies...

The issue is that go install puts the binary in $GOPATH/bin, but the PATH doesn't include $GOPATH/bin after installation. The GOPATH is set to /tmp/go, so the binary goes to /tmp/go/bin/goose, but the shell command just calls goose which is not in the PATH.

The fix: either use the full path /tmp/go/bin/goose or add $GOPATH/bin to PATH.

Let me fix the docker-compose.test.yml command:


command: >
  sh -c "go install github.com/pressly/goose/v3/cmd/goose@v3.20.0 &&
  export PATH=$PATH:/tmp/go/bin &&
  goose -dir /migrations postgres
  'postgres://gssr_test:gssr_test@postgres-test:5432/gssr_test?sslmode=disable' up"

и где в test фронтенд? почему migrate vendor не кэшируется?
The user has two questions:

"и где в test фронтенд?" - Where is the frontend in the test stack? The docker-compose.test.yml doesn't have a frontend service. The E2E tests (Playwright) test the API directly and need the frontend running. But looking at our current setup, the Playwright tests we wrote are API-level tests that hit the game API directly, not through a browser UI. So we don't need the frontend in the test stack for those tests.
However, if the user wants to test the full UI flow, they'd need the frontend running too. Let me check what we have...

Actually, looking at the current E2E tests (auth.spec.ts and game.spec.ts), they use request.newContext() to make direct API calls - they're API tests, not browser UI tests.

So the frontend isn't needed for these API-level tests, but if we wanted actual browser-based E2E testing, we'd need to either serve a built frontend statically or run the Vite dev server against the test API, which would add complexity to the test setup.

"почему migrate vendor не кэшируется?" - Why doesn't the migrate goose-cache not work? The goose-cache volume mounts at /tmp/go which is the GOPATH. When the container restarts, the goose binary should be in the cached volume, but there might be issues with how the cache volume is configured or where the binary is actually being stored.
The real problem is that GOMODCACHE is at /tmp/gomod which isn't in a named volume—it's ephemeral—so the module cache gets lost between runs. The goose-cache:/tmp/go volume caches the compiled binary at /tmp/go/bin/goose, but on the first run it still needs to download module sources, and on subsequent runs it should skip that step if the binary is already cached. The issue gets more complex when considering how go install resolves the full command with version specifiers.

A better approach would be to check if the binary already exists and only run go install if it doesn't, which avoids unnecessary module fetches and compilation when the cached binary is available. the binary existence check to skip the go install step entirely, which avoids needing GOMODCACHE caching. For the frontend question, the test stack currently only does API-level E2E tests without a frontend container, so I'm weighing whether to add a frontend-test service that builds and serves the frontend against the test API, or keep E2E tests API-focused and run UI tests separately against a dev server—Option 1 is more complete but adds complexity since the frontend needs additional configuration.

Looking at the actual test setup more carefully, the E2E tests use direct API calls through request.newContext() rather than browser interactions, so there's no frontend needed for the current test suite. The baseURL in the Playwright config points to the game API directly.

For the cache issue, I should check if the Go binary already exists before reinstalling it, and also make the Go module cache persistent with an additional volume mount.

Два отдельных вопроса — отвечаю по порядку.

1. Фронтенд в test-стеке

Его там нет намеренно. Текущие E2E-тесты (auth.spec.ts, game.spec.ts) используют request.newContext() — это прямые HTTP-запросы к API, без браузера и UI. Фронтенд нужен только для browser-based тестов (page.goto()).

Добавить — можно, но это значит собирать Vite-образ внутри docker-compose.test.yml. Нужно?

2. Почему goose-cache не работает

Проблема в том, что go install запускается каждый раз, даже если бинарь уже есть в томе. Нужно добавить проверку. Заодно GOMODCACHE тоже надо кэшировать — сейчас /tmp/gomod эфемерный:

Read c:\Users\catsi\Documents\GitHub\gssr\infra\compose\docker-compose.test.yml
Edit c:\Users\catsi\Documents\GitHub\gssr\infra\compose\docker-compose.test.yml
Added 2 lines
Edit c:\Users\catsi\Documents\GitHub\gssr\infra\compose\docker-compose.test.yml
Added 1 line
Готово. Теперь по сути изменений:

Было: go install goose → запускается всегда → скачивает модули каждый раз (GOMODCACHE был эфемерным)

Стало:

[ -f /tmp/go/bin/goose ] || go install ... — пропускает установку если бинарь уже есть
goose-bin:/tmp/go — кэш бинаря (был и раньше, просто переименован)
goose-mod:/tmp/gomod — новый том для кэша модулей Go
Важно: эти тома живут дольше чем сама БД. make test-down (= docker compose down -v) удаляет их тоже. Если хочешь сохранить кэш между прогонами, используй make test-down без флага -v:


# или вручную:
docker compose -f infra/compose/docker-compose.test.yml down   # тома сохраняются
docker compose -f infra/compose/docker-compose.test.yml down -v  # тома удаляются
